<Name>Troy Tiscareno<//Name><Time>1366163101158</Time><rating>4</rating><text>I went to Tailgaters for the first time on St. Patrick's Day 2013 for Happy Hour with about 8 friends. We ordered drinks/beer and $2 appetizers.

It's a sports bar, so there were sports on all of the 20 or so TVs, but it wasn't loud, so we could easily talk in our group.

Our waitress was attentive and checked up on is regularly, and kept the drinks and food coming. Not mind-blowing service or anything, but above average at least.

The appetizers were excellent. $2 (at Happy Hour) will get you 4 wings in any of a dozen or more flavors, 2 big potato skins, a small but reasonable plate of nachos, or several other items, and at those prices, you can afford to order a wide assortment and share, which is what we did. The wing sauces were all very good, and we tried at least 6 or 7 different ones. The potato skins were also very good.

Decor was fine, but typical mom & pop sports bar, nothing fancy. They do keep the place decently clean, though, which is a plus.

Overall, we had a great time, and I'm looking forward to the Antioch location opening, as it's very close to me. I'm not normally a big bar guy, but I'll definitely be spending some more time at Tailgaters.</text><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Response>

<pictures>None< /pictures>< Review>
I have been attending various churches for about 35 years.  Without a doubt Bayside Santa Rosa stands head and shoulders over all of them.  Centered around children's and youth ministries, Bayside for over two decades has flipped the script and has the youth leaders to prove it.

PLUS, they emphasize fidelity to the Word of God.   AND they reach out to the entire community through food distribution (2nd largest in Sonoma County), support for the homeless, service projects, outreach to the local schools.

Originally known as Redwood Covenant Church, we became part of Bayside Church after a two year transition, which in itself has been one of the most positive and rewarding experiences I have ever been through.

If you are seeking or looking for a church to belong to, please make certain you put Bayside Santa Rosa on your list.</Review>

<text>Iâ€™m still on the fence on this one.  On one hand I had a great experience wine tasting.   Food was tasty but left me quite hungry.  Had to go eat a real meal afterwards.

Let me explain.

About a dozen of you sit around a long circular bar type counter.  Owner/chef assembles small dishes that he pairs with wine.   Food is not cooked in front of you and is fairly easy to pull off.  Chef claims to have worked at a Michelin restaurant but these are not fancy dishes.

We had appetizers like sliced meats and cheese.  Also a warm soup.   Then came a chunk of salmon and a bit of steak.   Each dish was quite good but did not quite make a meal.  And Iâ€™m a small guy who typically does not eat much.

Each dish, however, was paired with a wine.  Wine education and pairing is the real strength here.    We had two kinds of bubblies, whites and reds.   They all quite good and paired really well.   When your glass was empty he would pour some more.   So that part was quite nice.

The seating is a bit peculiar.  Some people get the good seats and get to see what he is doing and others sit on the sides and donâ€™t get much of his attention.  The people who came the latest (the ones we all had to wait for) got the best seats so not sure how that works.

Part of the way through another group enters and they sit in a back room.   Now they get part of the chefâ€™s attention too.

Overall it was a fun experience. There was plenty of good wine to drink, but donâ€™t expect a filling meal.  Would I go back?   Yah, likely, but Iâ€™d eat first.< /text>< Pictures>

< username>
Tamara Scholtz< /username>

1521046594806< /date>

< Text>
I love walking into a new situation and not being exactly sure what I'm about to experience.  I love even more walking out thinking I can't WAIT to tell others that they need to experience this, too!

I think if people consider going to Somm's kitchen buying a ticket to an experience instead of paying a bill for dinner they'll get far more out of the ride.

On March 9, my husband and I were visiting Somm's kitchen from Austin, Texas.  We had been in Paso for the first time last year before this restaurant opened, so we were excited to try something new on the square.  We made a reservation about a month before.  When we walked in, Ian told us our spot was at the end of his semi circular bar which had enough room for about 14 people.

Ian greeted us and asked, "Are you hungry?"  We stated we were, and he handed us a glass of a most interesting Austrian sparkling wine.  We had no menu in front of us, wine or otherwise.  There was nothing to suggest what we might be eating, what we might be drinking, how many courses there may be, or even how much things might cost.

I'm sure we could have asked Ian, but we decided we were in for the ride!  For the next two hours we were in his hands as he had us try a local cheese, a foie gras that rivaled that of Michelin starred restaurants, a prime filet, lamb, and on and on...

It seemed some people came and went and didn't stay for the whole ride.  I'm not sure if all the kinks are ironed out there, but it didn't hinder our experience at all.

Each course was served with about a half of a glass of wine...unless of course you drank your wine, then more showed up.  None of the wines were particularly expensive, but all were particularly wonderful and the best paired I've ever had with any food ANYWHERE (and not to get all foodie/wine snobby... but we've been to Picasso, Cyrus, Robuchon... the pairing at Somm's Kitchen was simply AMAZING!)

The whole time we felt as though we were Ian's guests.  He chatted to us about the wines and the food and how he had prepared each thing.  At one point, he stopped and gave us a lesson in wine tasting.  It was taught in such a way that novice and experienced wine aficionados a like could enjoy. Ian is an experienced sommelier who teachers wine classes internationally, so getting a chance to experience this was quite a thrill!

In the French style, Ian prepared a salad between the final course and the desserts.  The salad was so creative.  He peeled the quail eggs and prepared it in front of us.  He carefully cut and placed herbs from right to left and as you ate, the herbs and the flavors increased in intensity with each bite.

We finished with desserts and feeling like we had made friends with our fellow diners and our host.

Our final bill was $250 for the two of us.  Both my husband and I felt this was truly a bargain.  We have paid more for less in the past.

Now, for the "to be completely honest" parts.  I would have liked a menu at least when we left if not to follow at the time.  Ian did say that I could email him and he would send a menu with all the information.  I intend to do that, but it would have been nice to look over it that evening, or even as I was writing this review.

Also, I'm not sure exactly how he decided who got what food.  There was a woman sitting next to me who I ran into twice again in the week while we were there.  Each time I saw her someplace else, she was telling other people that she was upset that she asked for potatoes and didn't get them even though some people did.  She did not like her experience at all and thought Ian was rude.  I thought he was funny and dry.  I liked his sense of humor, but I could see where others might find him off putting.  He's a New Yorker, not a Californian... and he still has some of the edge.

I also heard some complain about the price.   I think ANYWHERE you go 11 courses and 11 half glasses of wine for $125 a person is an amazing bargain... but I understand if you're thinking your'e only going to spend $50 on dinner.. this would be a little rough.</Text>

<Rating>4<//Rating>< Text>
I like it when places stick to what they are good at, and El Cora Birria is a perfect example of this.  No need to have 10 different meats, they just have beef/res  and goat/chivo, and thats all you need for choices here!

You know you are in for something good, when the parking lot is packed, a 4ft tall speaker (the kind with the flashing lights and a mixer built into the top), thumping away playing corrido songs.  And the taqueria is located inside a gas station/check cashing place.

the tacos were crispy and had a good flavor, I knocked it down one star only due to the fact I like my queso tacos a little cheesier than how they came, but they were still really good, and the green salsa they provided took it to another level.  If Yelp gave a option of a half star this place would be a solid 4.5 instead of a 4.

The consume was delicious, and about 1/4 of the cup was shredded beef on the bottom of it.  we saved ours to finish off later on.  We will 100% be back, I really want to try the mulitas next.<//Text>

< Text>
Male sure you call ahead to make sure they are open. They opened during the week for us as we made an appointment. It was $10 per person cash only so make sure you have it with you.

Overall a great little museum. Amazing selection of rare vintage bikes with little informative tidbits on each bike. Would recommend for any motorcyclists and fans.</Text>

<time>1514703146822</time>< review>
For the bargain price of $10.00 you can enter this exclusive museum which houses the private collection of Virgil Elings. This is an expansive collective of fine motorcycles.

Some of the featured items are 1910 FN to the present, and across all makes. Museum is geared toward the racing genre of motorcycles as it is aligned with the particular focus of Virgil and his son Jeff.

A visit to this museum is a delight and is a short trip from Los Angeles area through the drive along the coast to the beautiful Santa Ynez Valley.
Exhibits are diverse and do change as the seasons. Do visit.</review>

<user_id>110012963122389267086< /user_id><gmapID>0x80e954a0e39e4de9:0xc32641f119e7feaa<//gmapID><pictures>None< /pictures>< Review>
As a life long (half century and counting) motocycle enthusiast, it's always nice to find gems like this place.  The museum is a bit out of the way and hard to find but DEFINITELY worth it.  The quality of the bikes (BRITTEN, BMW KOMPRESSOR, CROCKER, BROUGH to name a few) was excellent.  The guy at the desk was a bit unique but even he couldn't ruin the excitment.  It would have helped had he known more about the bikes but I was left with the impression he got the job because he must know the owner.  Any more bikes and the museum will need to find more space as it is already way overcrowded with bikes.  To the owner, Sir, you have excellent taste.  Thank you for making your collection available to the masses.<//Review>

<Gmap_id>0x80db65e3fc49905d:0xcd5b9f95a4e11394</Gmap_id>< review>
Recently Joann fabrics moved from just east of downtown hemet to a new location on the west side of town.  What the reasons for the move are unclear. As the only full service cloth and sewers supply store within the city limits,  they hold the monopoly on the trade.
It may be to a general decline in overall sales as the days of mothers and daughters  sewing together are being replaced by lower cost garments available in the marketplace,  especially available online.
At one time,  women and some men,  relied on commercially available patterns to fabricate that specific piece of clothing that was not readily available in the local market.
Where the sewing machine was once a standard in every well kept home,  this device has been relegated into the hands of the occasional hobbyist.< /review>

It is a great place to shop if you don't mind that half the items on the shelves are not priced or priced correctly. My last visit some candles priced at 11.99 and a sign that says 25% off so the cost should be 8.99 but when you get to the register was told that the price was 15.99 and discounted to 11.99. There is a sign for the registers to start the line and wait for the next cashier that is open.
